|[http://youtrack.jetbrains.net/issue/TW-17167 TW-17167]
|Server
|Build might have "... is not fully resolved, using as is." warning with values with percentage signs that are reported from previous builds (e.g. NLSPATH case)
|If finish build parameters have percentage signs, they will be tried to be interpreted as references when used as dep.<br/><br/>Seems, the properties returned from a finish build should contain no references (all references should be escaped) and they should not be tried to be resolved anymore.<br/><br/>An example of default property with percentages on Linux: env.NLSPATH=    /usr/dt/lib/nls/msg/%L/%N.cat

|[http://youtrack.jetbrains.net/issue/TW-14803 TW-14803]
|plugin: Rake Runner
|RVM + Command line runner
|I recently upgraded to 6.0 and I'm psyched to see all of the rvm support, specifically the rvm ruby and gemset support for the rake runner and the ruby environment build feature.  There's one missing piece though, supporting rvm for the command line runner.<br/><br/>I have build plans and steps that invoke executables that are installed along with gems.  Some examples include cap (capistrano), bundle (bundler), and rspec.  There are other executables that are installed when gems are installed and it's not that uncommon to invoke them as part of a build.  A common build chain for our projects looks like this:<br/><br/>1) bundle install [command line runner]<br/>2) rake spec [rake runner]<br/>3) selenium script [command line runner]<br/>4) cap deploy [command line runner]<br/><br/>All of those steps depend on a specific rvm ruby and gemset.  There's currently no way to set the rvm ruby and gemset in one place for all of those steps.  The ruby environment build feature only applies to the rake runner.  In the above example, that's only one step.<br/><br/>There is an rvm command called "rvm-shell" that takes an argument for the ruby and gemset and executes a command given that env.  For example:<br/><br/>
<syntaxhighlight lang="text">
$ rvm-shell ruby-1.9.2@alder -c 'ruby -v; rvm gemset name'
ruby 1.9.2p0 (2010-08-18 revision 29036) [x86_64-darwin10.5.0]
alder
</syntaxhighlight><br/><br/>Using rvm-shell automatically for command line runners if the build plan includes the ruby environment build feature would solve the problem in an intuitive way without requiring additional options.  If that's too magic, then there could be an option on the command line runner screen, or a new runner called rvm-shell.<br/><br/>To be clear, my ultimate goal is to reduce the number of places where the rvm ruby and gemset are explicitly called out.  The ideal would be to set it once and have all aspects of the build use that setting, whether the step is using rake, a custom shell script, or one of the many executables installed by gems.  When that's possible in an easy and intuitive way, TeamCity's support for ruby projects will be officially kick ass.  That along with TW-14493 would be extra awesome.

|[http://youtrack.jetbrains.net/issue/WI-5789 WI-5789]
|PHP lang
|recogenise relative class names in PhpDoc
|PhpStorm uses PhpDoc to know the type of parameters and returned value by a function/method. However it seems not to work for namespace alias.<br/><br/>Consider the following:<br/>{code lang=php}<br/>namespace AppFoo;<br/>use AppBarMyClass;<br/>/**<br/>
* @return MyClass<br/>
*/<br/>public function getMyClass(MyClass $mc)<br/>{<br/>}<br/>{code}<br/><br/>While PhpStorm does recognize properly the alias (i.e. the type hint "MyClass" for $mc is "linked" to the alias as expected, and when using method getMyClass its parameter will be said to be of type AppBarMyClass), the return value will be incorrectly shown as AppFooMyClass (i.e. using the current namespace/ignoring the alias)<br/><br/>This unfortunately means that when a function returns a object of a specific class/interface, PhpStorm does not recognize it/list all methods available then.<br/><br/>(FYI if the function above had a tag "@param MyClass $mc" for the parameter, PhpStorm would then see it as either one: AppBarMyClass|AppFooMyClass)

For example, let's say I have a class named OneBigClass with two sets of logically related methods:<br/><br/>public class OneBigClass<br/>{<br/>private object _field1;<br/>private object _field2;<br/>public void DomainMethod1()<br/>{<br/>_field1 = 12345;<br/>}<br/>public void DomainMethod2()<br/>{<br/>_field1 = 54321;<br/>}<br/><br/>public void SomeOtherDomainMethod1()<br/>{<br/>_field2 = 12345;<br/>}<br/>public void SomeOtherDomainMethod2()<br/>{<br/>_field2 = 54321;<br/>}<br/>}<br/><br/>Ideally, what I would like R# to do is be able to let me choose which methods to extract into a separate class. For this example, let's assume that I wanted to extract methods DomainMethod1 and DomainMethod2. This is what the output should look like:<br/><br/>public class OneSmallerClass<br/>{<br/>private object _field1;<br/>public void DomainMethod1()<br/>{<br/>_field1 = 12345;<br/>}<br/>public void DomainMethod2()<br/>{<br/>_field1 = 54321;<br/>}<br/>}<br/><br/>The OneBigClass class should now look like this:<br/><br/>public class OneBigClass<br/>{<br/>private object _field1;<br/>private OneSmallerClass _smallClass = new OneSmallerClass();<br/>public void DomainMethod1()<br/>{<br/>_field1 = 12345;<br/>}<br/>public void DomainMethod2()<br/>{<br/>_field1 = 54321;<br/>}<br/><br/>public void SomeOtherDomainMethod1()<br/>{<br/>_smallClass.SomeOtherDomainMethod1();<br/>}<br/>public void SomeOtherDomainMethod2()<br/>{<br/>_smallClass.SomeOtherDomainMethod1();<br/>}<br/>}<br/><br/>Extract method is a good tool, but having to manually extract large classes can be quite tedious with the large codebases. Is there any way that you can pass this off to the Jetbrains R# devs? Thanks a lot, dude!<br/><br/><br/>Note by Hadi: If something like this were to be added, I'd give the option to inject the dependency instead of creating new instance.

    OutputStream stream = new FileOutputStream("asd");

      stream.close();

<syntaxhighlight lang="text">
  type DelayedClassificationDef = ((Entity.Value, Activity.Value), Duration)

  private var _scheduleDelayedClassifications: Seq[DelayedClassification] = Seq.empty

  def plant_schedule_delayed_classifications_=(delayedClassifications: Seq[DelayedClassificationDef]) {
    _scheduleDelayedClassifications = delayedClassifications.map(dc => DelayedClassification(dc._1._2, dc._1._1, dc._2))
  }
  def plant_schedule_delayed_classifications: Seq[DelayedClassificationDef] = throw new UnsupportedOperationException()
</syntaxhighlight><br/><br/>Use site<br/><br/>
<syntaxhighlight lang="text">
    plant_schedule_delayed_classifications = Seq(
      ((Entity.Operator, Activity.Break) -> 5.minutes)
      ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
      |
      Expression of type ((Entity.Value, Activity.Value), DurationBuilder) doesn't conform to type A
    )
</syntaxhighlight><br/><br/>5.minutes is really a DurationBuilder, which gets converted to Duration as needed. But the code compiles by scalac.

|[http://youtrack.jetbrains.net/issue/IDEA-74186 IDEA-74186]
|JavaScript
|JavaScript: Good code is red: Incorrect "Static member is not accessible"
|It is common practice to alias global names in a narrow scope to enable minification.<br/>Highcharts uses aliases to access function in Math:<br/>
<syntaxhighlight lang="text">(function(){
    var math = Math;
    var mathRound = math.round;
})();</syntaxhighlight><br/>That's perfectly valid, but IDEA highlights the ".round" with an error (that I cannot even suppress).

|[http://youtrack.jetbrains.net/issue/IDEA-75765 IDEA-75765]
|SQL
|SQL: PostgreSQL: FOREIGN KEY is red
|SQL, PostgreSQL.<br/>Seems that FOREIGN KEY table constraint is not parsed. Consider script:<br/>{code lang=sql}<br/>create table object_t(id integer primary key);<br/>create table subject_t(id integer primary key,<br/>rid1 integer,<br/>foreign key (rid1) references object_t, -- success, red<br/>rid2 integer references object_t);<br/>drop table subject_t;<br/>drop table object_t;<br/>{code}<br/>See the doc: http://www.postgresql.org/docs/9.1/interactive/sql-createtable.html<br/>IDEA reports error: see the comment in the sample above.<br/><br/>Same with FOREIGN KEY in the ALTER TABLE statement.<br/>110.162.
|-
|[http://youtrack.jetbrains.net/issue/IDEA-74629 IDEA-74629]
|JavaScript
|Fully implement the Console API
|Currently (as of PyCharm 2.0 EAP 108.1348 anyway), the Javascript skeleton and inspection only implements the <code>console.log</code> method of [the Console API|http://getfirebug.com/wiki/index.php/Console_API].<br/><br/>It would be nice and useful if it implemented the rest of the functions as well, or at least the well-supported ones:<br/>
* <code>console.debug</code>, <code>console.info</code>, <code>console.warn</code> and <code>console.error</code> which have the same signature as <code>console.log</code> (both forms)<br/>
* <code>console.assert</code>, which takes an expression to evaluate as its first parameter and otherwise behaves much like the first form of <code>console.log</code> (the one without a format string)<br/>
* <code>console.dir(Object)</code><br/>
* <code>console.dirxml(Node)</code><br/>
* <code>console.group(Object[, Object..]</code> and <code>console.groupCollapsed(Object[, Object..])</code> as well as <code>console.groupEnd()</code><br/>
* <code>console.trace()</code>, which simply prints the current traceback to the console<br/>
* <code>console.time(id:String)</code> and <code>console.timeEnd(id:String)</code> which take a single matching parameter (they can be interspersed, there should always be at least one <code>timeEnd</code> matching a called <code>time</code>)<br/>
* <code>console.profile([title:String])</code> and <code>console.profileEnd()</code><br/>
* <code>console.count([id:String])</code><br/><br/>There are also <code>console.exception(Error[, Object...])</code> and <code>console.table(Array<Array>|Array<Object>[, Array<String>|Array<Object>])</code>, but they don't seem implemented at all outside of Firebug

|Groovy/Grails
|Parameter name completion for Groovy DSL support
|I take advantages of the Groovy DSL support (as described in http://jetbrains.dzone.com/articles/custom-groovy-dsl-support), but I'm badly missing one feature. Namely, to be able to auto-complete parameter names.<br/><br/>In Groovy, one often defines a method like foo(Map,Closure) and then invoke it like foo(abc:1, def:2) { ... }. And it'd be mighty handy to be able to provide auto-completion for "abc" and "def" in this case. This pattern shows up in the markup builder, node builder, and ant builder. The *.gdsl files use this themselves to define method, property, and so on.

|[http://youtrack.jetbrains.net/issue/OC-2079 OC-2079]
|No subsystem
|Incorrect memory leak warning in custom object creation methods.
|According to cocoa memory guidelines, the object created by a method named copy* is owned by the caller of the method, not the class defining the method. With that in mind, the line in -[copyFoo] below is incorrectly flagged with a memory leak warning ("Retained value may not have been release"):<br/><br/>
<syntaxhighlight lang="text">
- (id)copyFoo {
  return [foo copy];
}
</syntaxhighlight><br/><br/>From [Apple's memory management guidelines:|http://developer.apple.com/library/mac/#documentation/Cocoa/Conceptual/MemoryMgmt/Articles/mmRules.html#//apple_ref/doc/uid/20000994-SW1]<br/>{quote}<br/>'''You own any object you create'''<br/>You create an object using a method whose name begins with “alloc”, “new”, “copy”, or “mutableCopy” (for example, alloc, newObject, or mutableCopy).<br/>{quote}

|NOTE: Please edit the summary, after reading this to something more meaningful :)<br/><br/>I've attached 2 classes: Foo and Bar.<br/>Foo has a property from type Bar, but in Foo.h there is only a @class Bar and not an #import Bar.h .<br/><br/>Trying to access Bar's members using any type of auto-complete results a "No suggestion" popup (see attached screenshot).<br/>The solution is to:<br/>1. |[http://youtrack.jetbrains.net/issue/OC-2087 OC-2087]
|No subsystem
|AppCode incorrectly showing variables not released in dealloc
|In UIViewController code, the paradigm is to do:<br/><br/>- (void)dealloc<br/>{<br/>[self viewDidUnload];<br/><br/>[super dealloc];<br/>}<br/><br/>'view' variables are supposed to be released in viewDidUnload, which is called from dealloc.  AppCode is reporting that the variables (which are released in viewDidUnload), are not released, even though they are, through the call to viewDidUnload in the dealloc method.  AppCode should be smart about what dealloc is calling before it reports certain variables are not being released.

|[http://youtrack.jetbrains.net/issue/IDEA-74852 IDEA-74852]
|No subsystem
|PostgreSQL: unsupported syntax for SELECT INTO ... in stored procedures
|all of these are valid in pl/pgsql, but an error is displayed in editor:<br/><br/>
<syntaxhighlight lang="sql">
-- no error displayed:
SELECT SUM(price) INTO a_total_price FROM Product;

-- reverse order is allowed too (editor error: expression required)
SELECT INTO a_total_price SUM(price) FROM Product;

-- multiple targets are valid as well (editor error: unexpected ',' after a_total_price)
SELECT SUM(price), COUNT(*) INTO a_total_price, a_product_count FROM Product;

-- INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE can return expressions too (editor error: unexpected 'INTO')
INSERT INTO Barcode(product_id, barcode) VALUES (13515, '165165161') RETURNING barcode_pk INTO l_barcode_pk;

</syntaxhighlight><br/><br/>more info: http://www.postgresql.org/docs/8.2/static/plpgsql-statements.html#PLPGSQL-STATEMENTS-SQL-ONEROW<br/><br/>thank you

|[http://youtrack.jetbrains.net/issue/KT-377 KT-377]
|
|Prohibit 'super' as a receiver argument to extension functions
|
<syntaxhighlight lang="text">
trait T {
    fun foo() {}
    fun buzz() {}
    fun buzz1(i : Int) {}
}

fun T.bar() {}

fun any(a : Any) {}

fun T.buzz() {}
fun T.buzz1() {}

class C : T {
    fun test() {
        fun T.buzz() {}
        fun T.buzz1() {}
        super.foo() // OK
        super.bar() // Error
        super.buzz() // OK, resolved to a member
        super.buzz1() // Resolved to a member, but error: no parameter passed where required
        any(super) // not an expression
        if (super) {} else {} // not an expression
        val x = super // not an expression
        when (1) {
            super => 1 // not an expression
        }
    }
}
</syntaxhighlight>

This is caused by a XamlParseException xClassNotDerivedFromElement caused by the x:Class attribute added to the Xaml Theme file.  Deleting the attribute from the Theme xaml corrects the problem.

|[http://youtrack.jetbrains.net/issue/TW-14103 TW-14103]
|Server
|Errors accessing buildAgent.zip by the server can result in all agents marked as "outdated"

|No subsystem
|Structural Search and Replace doesn't want to replace something with extension methods
|I have implemented an extension-method like this (I think the code is easier to read this way):<br/>
<syntaxhighlight lang="text">public static bool IsNullOrEmpty(this string subject) {
    return String.IsNullOrEmpty(subject); }</syntaxhighlight><br/><br/>I have also created a search and replace pattern in the pattern catalog:<br/>
<syntaxhighlight lang="text">  <Pattern Severity="WARNING" FormatAfterReplace="True" ShortenReferences="True" Language="CSHARP">
    <Comment>Use a more readable version of string.IsNullOrEmpty()</Comment>
    <ReplaceComment>Use extensionmethod .IsNullOrEmpty() instead</ReplaceComment>
    <ReplacePattern>$var$.IsNullOrEmpty()</ReplacePattern>
    <SearchPattern>$expr$.IsNullOrEmpty($var$)</SearchPattern>
    <Params />
    <Placeholders>
      <IdentifierPlaceholder Name="var" Type="" ExactType="False" RegEx="" CaseSensitive="True" />
      <ExpressionPlaceholder Name="expr" ExpressionType="System.String" ExactType="True" />
    </Placeholders>
  </Pattern>
</syntaxhighlight><br/>The pattern matches fine, but when I try to replace (either through searching from the pattern catalog, or via the QuickFix lightbulb menu) on the following code:<br/><br/>
<syntaxhighlight lang="text">// text is of type string
if (!String.IsNullOrEmpty(text))
{
    // statements
}</syntaxhighlight><br/><br/>I end up with this code:<br/><br/>
<syntaxhighlight lang="text">if (!String.IsNullOrEmpty())
{
    // statements
}</syntaxhighlight><br/><br/>while I expected this code:<br/><br/>
<syntaxhighlight lang="text">if (!text.IsNullOrEmpty())
{
    // statements
}</syntaxhighlight><br/><br/>If i replace my extension-method with one of String's built-in methods (like .IsNormalized()), the replacing works as expected.

|[http://youtrack.jetbrains.net/issue/RSRP-277343 RSRP-277343]
|No subsystem
|"Property hides enum from outer class" appears to be incorrect
|I had some code like this:<br/><br/>
<syntaxhighlight lang="text">
public class Outer {
    public enum MyEnum { Zero, One, Two };
    public class Inner {
        public MyEnum MyEnum { get; set; }
    }
}
</syntaxhighlight><br/><br/>ReSharper showed a blue squiggly underline under the "MyEnum" property name, with tooltip "Property 'MyEnum MyEnum' hides enum from outer class".<br/><br/>This is not a valid / meaningful message. This property doesn't hide anything; it doesn't prevent me from working with the enum in any way. If I want to write code in my Inner class that works with the MyEnum type, I can -- there's nothing stopping me from referring to MyEnum.Zero inside my inner class, or referring to typeof(MyEnum) or List<MyEnum>.<br/><br/>If the property were of a '''different''' type -- say, "public string MyEnum { get; set; }" -- then the warning would make sense, because then I would be unable to refer to the MyEnum type from my inner class. But because the type is the same as the property name, the compiler has no trouble figuring things out, and ReSharper's warning is incorrect.<br/><br/>ReSharper shouldn't show this warning when the property type is the same as the property name.

|[http://youtrack.jetbrains.net/issue/MPS-14513 MPS-14513]
|Typesystem
|Performance issues with Type System rules
|Currently, all type system rules as well as the NonTypesystemRules are executed "autoamtically" if something changes. For large models, this can be come a performance problem.<br/><br/>This could be solved by marking a rule as RUN_ON_CHANGE or RUN_ONLY_IN_CHECKER.<br/><br/>Rules with RUN_ON_CHANGE are checked in realtime, just as now. RUN_ONLY_IN_CHECKER is only checked if the model checker is run by the user.

|plugin: FxCop
|Problem setting custom ruleset for fxcop (vs2010)
|I have a custom ruleset for fxCop in vs2010 (it's included in the 2010 installation) that I am able to run in an msbuild script with no problem, but trying to get the fxCop runner to work with it has failed me. I tried adding it to the "extra parameters", but I can't get parameter expansion to work correctly (since it requires the rules directory to be specified. It's in a path with spaces (I can't help that because it's in program files), but if I include spaces around the parameter (like /r:"%env.fxCopPath%/Rules") every variation on that results in parameter errors. Without quotes it treats each space in the parameter like another parameter, but with quotes it never seems to expand correctly. To properly use FxCop, we really need to be able to specify rulesets (/rs:+/-/=) and paths to rule assemblies and folders (/r:)

|[http://youtrack.jetbrains.net/issue/TW-8427 TW-8427]
|plugin: FxCop
|FxCop: Incorrect handling of doublequotes in "Additional FxCopCmd options"
|from http://www.jetbrains.net/devnet/thread/282122?tstart=0<br/><br/>The "Additional FxCopCmd options" textbox incorrectly handles doublequotes. To replicate:<br/><br/><br/>In the FxCop runner configuration, enter the following into the "Additional FxCopCmd options" textbox: /d:References1 /d:References2<br/><br/>Save and run the build configuration.<br/><br/>Verify (via the Build Log) that fxcopcmd was executed with the correct arguments.<br/><br/>In the FxCop runner configuration, change /d:References1 to /d:"My References".<br/><br/>Save and run the build configuration.<br/><br/>Check the Build Log again.<br/><br/><br/>This time you will see that instead of the arguments looking like<br/><br/>/d:"My References" /d:References2<br/><br/>... you will see:<br/><br/>"/d:"My References"" /d:References2<br/><br/>(Note the extraneous doublequotes around the first parameter.)

|[http://youtrack.jetbrains.net/issue/RSRP-277342 RSRP-277342]
|Code Analysis - Find Code Issues
|Warning for delegate instance creation from base.-referenced method group inside closure/iterator
|To prevent this kind of things:<br/><br/>{code lang=csharp}<br/>using System;<br/><br/>class Boo {<br/>public event Action Event = () => { };<br/>public void Fire() { Event(); }<br/>}<br/><br/>class FooBase {<br/>public virtual void Bar() {<br/>Console.WriteLine("FooBase.Bar");<br/>}<br/>}<br/><br/>class Foo : FooBase {<br/>public void DomSmth(Boo boo) {<br/>boo.Event += base.Bar;<br/>new Action(() => boo.Event -= base.Bar)();<br/>boo.Fire();<br/>}<br/>}<br/><br/>class Program {<br/>static void Main() {<br/>new Foo().DomSmth(new Boo());<br/>}<br/>}<br/>{code}<br/>This is because compiler emits wrapper method for <code>base.</code> calls from closures. So the delegate equality will not work and created delegate will not be equal to other delegate instance from <code>base.Bar</code>.

|Typesystem

|[http://youtrack.jetbrains.net/issue/RSRP-238699 RSRP-238699]
|No subsystem
|Add support for code contracts
|It would be nice if R# had some quick fixes and refactorings that makes working with code contracts easier.<br/><br/>I'd like to see the following features:<br/><br/>1) "Generate contract class for interface" refactoring<br/>Code Contracts for interfaces have to be placed in an abstract class, as the interface does not have method bodies where the contract calls could be placed. It would be nice if R# could generate such a class for me.<br/><br/>2) "Move contract to contract class" quick fix<br/>Sometimes I forget to place the contracts of a method in the contract class, and place them in the class that implements the interface instead. ReSharper should warn me about that and offer to move the contracts to the contract class. It could also create the contract class if it does not exist yet.<br/><br/>3) "Extract Interface" refactoring should generate a contract class if the methods that are extracted to an interface contain code contracts.

|Resolve
|Paths like 'C.super' are unresolved
|The following code compiles and runs well:<br/><br/>
<syntaxhighlight lang="text">
class A {
	def doSmth = {}
}
class B extends A {
	override def doSmth = {}
	B.super.doSmth	// error: 'Cannot resolve symbol B'
	B.this.doSmth	// ok
}

|REST API
|Is it possible to return some metrics on a filter result rather than the full dump of the issues?
|Hi,<br/>Using our current isue tracker (fortress) we display a dashboard of metrics in mediawiki.  There are many advantages to embedding dynamic data from the issuetracker within wiki articles, and it is a cornerstone of our process.  It works very well, and I need to replicate this with youtrack as the back end.<br/><br/>Here is an example of a wiki page displaying some dynamic data.  Each time the page is rendered, it connects to fortress, and extracts the information.<br/><br/>I guess I could do this with the current REST API, but it would be more efficient if YT had a method to return the filter result ''count'' rather than the actual records.  This becomes important if you have hundreds or thousands of issues, as your max limit starts to become a problem, and the whole thing slows down to a crawl.<br/><br/>specifically, I would like;<br/>
* A method to return the '''count''' from a a filter query<br/>
* The '''sum''' of a a ''numeric field'' (e.g. time estimates) from a filter query<br/><br/>!screenshot1.png!<br/><br/>FYI, here are the actual issues in a wiki article.  you can see the duration at the bottom of the table.  I have noted that YT is a fair bit slower than fortress (SQLserver) at extracting records from its DB, but I need to make some more detailed tests before I formally report this.<br/><br/>!screenshot2.png!
